The staff at Just Ride LA are fantastic. They were the most helpful, understanding and reasonably-priced bike shop to disassemble two bikes for shipping across the country (my partner and I called at least five other bike shops in the area). < text>
I never knew Rallys was a nationwide chain. This gave me memories of the time I spend my summer with my relatives in the San Diego County town of Ramona back in 2001. The one in Ramona is no longer there, but there is one in Escondido. Who knew, I would eat at Rallys again a few decades later. This Rallys opened not too long ago. This one is a full restaurant with drive thru, the one in Ramona and Escondido is a drive thru with a few outdoor picnic tables.

I ordered a Big Bufford. Its was pretty good. It had a little bit of In N Out flavor, but its own thing. The one I ate in Ramona was the regular hamburger which had a sesame seed bun. The fries tasted like seasoned curly fries. My sister ate a Spicy Chicken sandwich, which I will try next time.

4 Stars.< /text>

<user_id>114159077503843424232</user_id>< Name>
valen zuela</Name>
<time>1563556525065< /time><rating>3< /rating>< text>
Finally got around to trying Luisa and Sons in Cerritos. They're situated in strip lot on South Street, next to Cafe 86. It's a small bakery serving up classic Filipino pastries and desserts like egg pie, cassava, turon, sponge cake mamon and many more. What caught my eye was their display case of hopia which I heard was good. They have several selections on hand like mung bean, red bean, ube and baboy (made out of pork fat, candied winter melon and green onions).

I decided to try a dozen ube hopia (85 cent each) and half dozen chicken empanadas. The chicken empanadas were tasty and crust was on point, but unfortunately their ube hopia was a complete disappointment. The ube flavor was lacking and quality of crust wasn't flaky. Both essential characters to good hopia. it just tasted like standard pastries without any soul and originality.

All in all, the experience was okay. The hopia place near my house is so much better. Return visit is unlikely, but if you decide to come here anyways skip the ube hopia.

Note: For some nutritional facts, mongo or mung bean helps lower blood cholesterol levels, helps prevent breast cancer and also it has low sugar level. So if ever you are on a strict diet, this hopia mongo will surely be a good pick. Make sure to mention that to your doctor. Hahaha!< /text>

<user_id>102918253898437847981<//user_id><Name>Rodney S< /Name><Time>1416199019771<//Time><rating>4<//rating><review>Lotta empanada for da dolla, I holla!

Just $0.60 gets you one of these bad boys, the Pilipino chicken empanada
Flaky, sweet, savory & oh so delicious!  Tender pieces of chicken, carrots and raisins stuffed inside a buttery crust.  I can polish off about 75 of these during one sitting ;p

Luisa & Sons is a Pilipino bakeshop offering traditional cuisine from the homeland, both savory & sweet.

Fresh baked goods are prepared daily & gobbled up by the masses

Have a sweet tooth?  No problem!  Luisa & Sons offers delectable treats to satisfy your sugar fix

Besides the sweets & baked goods, savory dishes are available for purchase in the freezers and for pre-order food trays, such as sisig & dinuguan.  My family has often ordered a tray of pancit malabon (Pilipino noodle dish) & a box of empanadas for special occasions.  They're always a hit & nary a leftover afterwards.

Service has always been good.  I'm a regular, so the staff already knows they have to restock their supplies once I'm done shopping ;p

Parking is in the Unimart shopping plaza, shared with Milk & Honey, Azon & Canaan restaurants, among others.

What da bloody heck ya waitin for?  Go to Luisa & Sons Bakeshop already!

Highly recommend!

<Rate>5< /Rate>< review>
Excellent! I read an ad and short promotional article; it was not exaggerated. Place is inviting, clean, and bright. We went for late lunch about 230 pm. All menu items were available. Staff was friendly and attentive and answered all our questions regarding items not familiar to us. We settled on a toasted ham sandwich and side salad and Havana Burrito. Both were excellent! The greens were fresh, the sourdough bread was fresh, the pulled pork in the burrito was juicy and the black beans and rice with bacon absolutely scrumptious! I liked the twist of a fried egg on top. The side salsa was so tasty, not just overwhelming with chili peppers. I also had a perfect Mojito. We will return for another meal!<//review>

<text>The best part of my dinner was the coffee.  I wanted to order from the lunch menu, but the waiter told me that I could only order from the dinner menu at that time (about 5:45).  I have been there several other times, and was always allowed to order a sandwich from the lunch menu, nearly at the same time in the late afternoon, (mainly because I did not like the dinner menu choices). So, I ordered from the dinner menu anyway. After ordering, just next to me was a couple, and right in front of me, he brought their dinner, and the lady had a sandwich that looked like a club sandwich (or turkey club). Now, I hardly ever complain, but he has done this to me before.  I guess that I am not considered equal to the other customers. 113513189030654208545</user_id>
<name>Libby Kauper</name><Time>1546807153315</Time><Rating>5< /Rating>< text>
Rick's Desert Grill is a good eatery you can always count on. The dishes are fresh, straight forward, some with a Cuban flair, and the staff are super friendly. They also serve cocktails.  It's located on the north end of Palm Canyon Drive, and I often go there after arriving late to Palm Springs when I know other restaurants are full, or I just want a non-pretentious, relaxing environment .
Rick's begins every dinner with complimentary deviled eggs, a very retro and homey touch. You immediately feel you're in the smaller Palm Springs zone. I often start with one of their tasty home made soups, which they also serve at Rick's Deli up the road. The menu features grilled salmon, fried chicken, Aroz con Pollo, and turkey dinners, too.  It has something for everyone without being a huge menu.
Rick's also displays wonderful black and white photography of historical Palm Springs from the 1930's-50's, featuring a beautiful Lucille Ball in palazzo pants, Bob Hope holding a ham, Cary Grant lounging in his pool, and many others. It's all very understated and comfortable.
Although I often visited Rick's other eatery, Rick's Deli, for their amazing breakfasts and lunches, I would always pass the Desert Grill because it looked sterile on the outside and was located on the corner of a busy intersection. Once I went, it soon became a favorite. I am glad Rick's Desert Grill has become one of my staples in Palm Springs.</text>

<user>106401336386212612082<//user><user_name>E< /user_name>< date>

<Rate>5< /Rate>< Review>
I drive pass by this place so many times while taking my son to school and it never occur to me to stop by because of the outer appearance.  In a nutshell, the food is great and the mojito is to die for!  My husband ordered a grilled ribeye and I ordered a pull pork dish.  They both came out wonderful.  The meat is so moist and juicy.  The rice with beans and plantain on the side were a nice touch.  My 2 year old, who's usually a very picky eater, loved the squash soup that came with the pulled pork.  He drank more than half in less than 5 minutes!  The food taste so good here, they honestly don't need to worry about decoration or anything else.</Review>
